тАШ рдкреНрд░рд╛рд╡реЗрдкрд╛рдГ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рдЪрддреБрд░реНрджрд╢рд░реНрдЪрдВ рдкрдЮреНрдЪрдордВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдореИрд▓реВрд╖рд╕реНрдп рдХрд╡рд╖рд╕реНрдпрд╛рд░реНрд╖рдВ рдореБрдЬрд╡рддрдГ рдкреБрддреНрд░рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдХреНрд╖рд╛рдЦреНрдпрд╕реНрдп рд╡рд╛ред рд╕рдкреНрддрдореА рдЬрдЧрддреА рд╢рд┐рд╖реНрдЯрд╛рд╕реНрддреНрд░рдпреЛрджрд╢ рддреНрд░рд┐рд╖реНрдЯреБрднрдГ ред рдЕрддреНрд░ рджреНрд╡рд╛рджрд╢реА рдЕрдХреНрд╖рд╛рдиреН рд╕реНрддреМрддрд┐ рдирд╡рдореНрдпрд╛рджреНрдпрд╛ рдЪ рд╕рдкреНрддрдореА ред рдЕрддрд╕реНрддрджреНрджреЗрд╡рддреНрдпрд╛рдГ ред рддреНрд░рдпреЛрджрд╢реА рдХреГрд╖рд┐рдВ рд╕реНрддреМрддрд┐ ред рдЕрддрд╕реНрддрд╕реНрдпрд╛рдГ рд╕рд╛ рджреЗрд╡рддрд╛ ред рдПрд╡рдВ рдкрдЮреНрдЪ рдЧрддрд╛рдГ ред рд╢рд┐рд╖реНрдЯрд╛рднрд┐рд░реНрдирд╡рднрд┐рдГ рдХрд┐рддрд╡реЛрд╜рдХреНрд╖рд╛рд╢реНрдЪ рдирд┐рдиреНрджреНрдпрдиреНрддреЗ ред рдЕрддрд╕реНрддрд╛ рдЕрдкрд┐ рддрджреНрджреЗрд╡рддреНрдпрд╛рдГ ред рддрдерд╛ рдЪрд╛рдиреБрдХреНрд░рд╛рдиреНрддрдВ — тАШ рдкреНрд░рд╛рд╡реЗрдкрд╛рдГ рд╖рд│реВрдирд╛ рдореМрдЬрд╡рд╛рдиреНрд╡рд╛рдХреНрд╖реЛрд╜рдХреНрд╖рдХреГрд╖рд┐рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рд╛ рдЪрд╛рдХреНрд╖рдХрд┐рддрд╡рдирд┐рдиреНрджрд╛ рдЪ рд╕рдкреНрддрдореА рдЬрдЧрддреА ’ рдЗрддрд┐ ред рдЧрддреЛ рд╡рд┐рдирд┐рдпреЛрдЧрдГ редред

Jamison Brereton

34 (860)
Gambler
Kavaс╣гa Ail┼лс╣гa or Akс╣гa Maujavant
14 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh, except jagat─л 7
One of the most famous, most translated, and most anthologized hymns in the R╠еgveda, this lively and vivid lament of the gambler depicts the sad lot of a man addicted to dicing but unsuccessful at it. This hapless speaker describes the intoxi cation that grips him when he is playing or even contemplating play and that leaves him helpless to resist (vss. 1, 5тАУ9), as well as the toll this compulsion takes on his personal life and the self-pity this evokes in him (vss. 2тАУ4, 10тАУ11). At the end of the hymn the gambler vows to renounce play (vs. 12), and the god Savitar restores him to his former position (vs. 13). The final verse (14) is the gamblerтАЩs address to the dice, urging them to leave him alone and find another victim. This portion of the

hymn has the form of a ritual expiation, embodied especially in the last words of 12d, in which the gambler avows the truth of his speech.
Dicing was an important cultural feature of ancient India, especially associ ated with kings and the ruling class. Already in middle Vedic sacrifice, in the R─Бjas┼лya, the ritual of the consecration of the king, there is a ritual dicing match, rigged so that the king-to-be wins. Of course, the whole of the great epic, the Mah─Бbh─Бrata, is determined by the outcome of the dicing match between Yudhiс╣гс╣нhira and his cousins: Yudhiс╣гс╣нhira gambles away his kingdom, his broth ers, his wife, and himself and must fight to regain his kingship. The much-loved story of Nala and Damayant─л also involves the gambling away of a kingdom, this time by Nala. And the dharma texts consider gambling, along with hunting and womanizing, to be a characteristic pursuitтАФand viceтАФof kings (cf. M─Бnava Dharma ┼Ъ─Бstra VII.47, 50; for condemnation of gambling in general see, e.g., MD┼Ъ IX.220тАУ28).
Ancient Indian dicing was quite different from the game that the word con jures up in the modern mind, and much scholarship has been devoted to figur ing out what the play actually consisted of (see, e.g., Lu╠Иders 1907; Falk 1986). It seems to have involved a large quantity of a particular kind of nut (vibh─лdaka /vibh─лtaka) as the dice; these had no markings on them. They were thrown into a hollow on the ground, and the players took turns pulling out a handful. The best тАЬhandтАЭ was one divisible by four, and the other hands were ranked accord ing to how many nuts were left over after a division by four, with a single leftover nut being the worst (see vs. 2c). For details, see Falk (1986: 73тАУ133). Although it may be hard for us to imagine the passions enflamed by this kind of long division, our own games of chance probably will not stand up to scrutiny some millennia in the future.
The monologue form found here is almost unprecedented in the R╠еgveda, and the shifting play of emotionsтАФguilty excitement, tender remembrance of his past life and family, scorn for his own weakness and the disgust he arouses in others, bitter anger at the inanimate dice that brought him low, to which he ascribes agency and malign intention and for which he still longsтАФis psychologi
cally convincing and very moving. Showing our own biases, we might proudly deem it quite тАЬmodern.тАЭ

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe large rattling dice exhilarate me as torrents borne on a precipice flowing in a desert; the excitingdice animate me as the taste of the Soma of Maujavat (delights the gods).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Flowing in a desert: iriс╣Зevarvс╣Ыt─Бnaс╕е: a reference to the dice; rolling on the dice-board; exciting dice: vibh─лtaka, the seed of themyrobalan, used as a die;

Maujavat: a mountain, where is said the best Soma is found

Jamison Brereton

The dangling (nuts) of the lofty (tree) exhilarate me, the ones born in a windy place, constantly whirling in the gaming hollow.
Like a draught of soma from Mt. M┼лjavant, the wakeful vibh─лdaka nut has pleased me.

Griffith

SPRUNG from tall trees on windy heights, these rollers transport me as they turn upon the table.
The enlivening Vibh─лdaka has pleased me like the draught of Soma from M┼лjavant.

Macdonell

On high trees born and in a windy region The danglers, rolling on the diceboard, cheer me. Like Soma draught from M┼лjavant’s great mountain, The rousing nut Vibh─лdaka has pleased me.

Geldner

Die Ohrenbommeln des hohen Baums, die im Sturmwind geborenen, berauschen mich, wenn sie in der Rinne trudeln. Wie ein Trunk Soma vom Berge Mujavat deuchte mir der wach haltende Vibhidakaw├╝rfel.

Grassmann

Die h├╝pfenden aus luft’gem Wipfel stammend berauschen mich, wenn in der Bahn sie rollen, Wie der Genuss des Maudschawater Soma’s d├╝nkt lustig des Vibh─лdakbaumes Nuss mir.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThis (my wife) has not been angry (with me), nor was she overcome with sham; kind was she to meand to my friends; yet for the sake of one or other die, I have deserted this affectionate spouse.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

She did not oppose me, nor did she get angry; she was gracious to my comrades and to me.
I, on account of one die too many, have pushed away my avowed wife.

Griffith

She never vexed me nor was angry with me, but was ever gracious to my friends and me.
For a dice which scored one too much, I drive away my own devoted wife.

Macdonell

She wrangles not with me nor is she angry: To me and comrades she was ever kindly. For dice that only luckless throws effected I’ve driven away from home a wife devoted.

Geldner

Grassmann

Nie reizte mich, noch z├╝rnte mir die Gattin, sie war mir hold, mir selbst und meinen Freunden; Des W├╝rfels halb, der durch ein Aug’ entscheidet, verstiess ich die mir treuergebne Gattin.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMy mother-in-law reviles me, my wife opposes me; the beggar meets no compassionate (benefactor); Ido not realize the enjoyment of the gamester any more than that of a valuable horse grown old.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Her mother-in-law [=my mother] hates me; my wife pushes me away. A man in distress finds no one to pity him. тАЬI find no more use for a gambler than for an old nag up for sale,тАЭ (so they say).

Griffith

My wife drives me away, her mother hates me: the wretched man finds none to give him comfort.
[They say:] “I find no more use in a gambler than in an aged horse which is for sale.”

Macdonell

Her mother hates me, she herself rejects me: For one in such distress there is no pity. I find a gambling man is no more useful Than is an aged horse that’s in the market.

Geldner

Die Schwiegermutter ist mir feind, die Gattin st├╢├Яt mich von sich. In Not geraten, findet der Spieler keinen Erbarmer: Ich finde an dem Spieler keinen Nutzen, so wenig wie an einem alten verk├дuflichen Pferd.

Grassmann

Mich hasst die Schwieger, mich verl├дsst die Gattin, und der bedr├дngte findet kein Erbarmen; Auch find’ ich nicht, wozu der Spieler nutze, gleich wie ein Ross, das theuer, aber alt ist.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬOthers touch the wife of him whose wealth the potent dice covet; his mother, father, brothers say, “weknow him not, take him away bound (where you will)".тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Touch the wife: parimс╣Ы┼Ыanti: they drag her by her clothesor her hair

Jamison Brereton

Others fondle the wife of a man whose possessions the die with eyes on the prize has hungered for.
Father, mother, brothers say about him, тАЬWe do not know him; lead him away bound.тАЭ

Griffith

Others embrace the wife of him whose riches the victorious dice have coveted:
Father and mother and brothers say about him [to the landlord’s men]: “We know him not: tie him up and take him away.”

Macdonell

Others embrace the wife of him whose chattels The eager dice have striven hard to capture; And father, mother, brothers say about him: “We know him not; lead him away a captive.”

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWhen I relect, (then I say), “I will plural y no more with them”. I pay attention to my friends who desert(me); and the tawny dice rattle as they are thrown; I hasten to their accusative tomed plural ce as a harlot (to anassignation).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

When I resolve, тАЬI will not play with them,тАЭ I am bereft of my
comrades, who go off (without me).
And as soon as, scattered down, the brown (dice) have raised their
voice, I just go to their appointed place, like a girl with a lover.

Griffith

When I resolve “I will not play with them, I will remain behind when my friends [= fellow-gamblers] depart [to play]”,
and the brown dice, thrown on the board, have rattled, like a fond girl I seek the place of meeting.

Macdonell

When to myself I think, “I’ll not go with them, I’ll stay behind my friends that go to gamble,” And those brown nuts, thrown down, have raised their voices, I go, like wench, straight to the place of meeting.

Geldner

Wenn ich mir vornehme: ich will nicht mehr mit ihnen spielen, ich bleibe hinter den fortgehenden Kameraden zur├╝ck - und wenn die geworfenen Braunen ihre Stimme erheben, so eile ich doch zu ihrem Stelldichein wie eine Buhlin.

Grassmann

Und wenn ich denk’: nicht will ich ferner spielen, so weichen von mir alle meine Freunde; Und h├╢r ich dann die braunen W├╝rfel fallen, so eil’ ich wie zum Stelldichein die Buhle.

English translation:

тАЬThe gamester goes to the gambling table, radiant in person n, and asking himself, “Shall I win?” Thedice increase his passion for plural y as he practises the arts of (gambling) with his adversary.тАЭ

Shall I win: askingwhat rich man is here; I shall beat him

Jamison Brereton

The gambler goes to the hall of play asking himself, тАЬwill I win?тАЭ puffing himself up with тАЬI will win!тАЭ
The dice run counter to his desire, conferring the winning throws on his opponent.

Griffith

The gamester seeks the gambling-house, and wonders, his body all afire, “Will I be lucky?”
The dice run against his desire, giving the best throws to his adversary.

Macdonell

To the assembly hall the gambler sallies. And asking, “Shall I win?” he quakes and trembles. And then the dice run counter to his wishes, Giving the lucky throw to his opponent.

Geldner

Grassmann

Ins Spielhaus geht der Spieler voll Begierde, ┬╗heut sieg’ ich┬л, spricht er, auf sich selbst vertrauend; Die W├╝rfel steigern h├╢her sein Begehren, was er gewonnen, setzt er ein dem Gegner.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬDice verily are armed with hooks, with goads, pricking, paining and torturing (the gamester); to thewinning (plural yer) they are the givers of sons, they are tipped with honey; slaying him in return by taking away thegambler’s (all).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

They are the givers of sons: by acquiring wealth through their means a family may be reared; bytaking the gambler’s all: barhaс╣Зa = parivс╣Ыddheс╣Зa sarvasvaharaс╣Зena

Jamison Brereton

They are just тАЬdiceтАЭтАФbut hooking, goading, debasing, scorching, seeking to scorch,
giving (temporarily) like a child, then in turn slapping down the victor, infused with honey, with power over the gambler.

Griffith

Dice, verily, are armed with goads and driving-hooks, deceiving and tormenting, causing grievous woe.
They give gifts like boys [do], and then snatch them back from the winner,
[they are] sweetened [as] with honey with magic power over the gambler.

Macdonell

The dice attract the gambler, but deceive and wound, Both paining men at play and causing them to pain. Like boys they offer first and then take back their gifts: With honey sweet to gamblers by their magic charm.

Geldner

Die W├╝rfel haben Widerhaken, Stacheln; sie sind Vereitler, Qu├дler, Qu├дlgeister. Ihre Geschenke sind wie die der Kinder; sie schlagen den Sieger wieder. Durch des Spielers ├Ьbereifer sind sie mit Honig durchtr├дnkt.

Grassmann

Die W├╝rfel sind anhakend und sich einbohrend, knechtend, brennend, marternd, nur kurzes Gl├╝ck gew├дhrend, den Sieger dann wieder schlagend; und doch mit S├╝ssigkeit vermischt durch Bezauberung des Spielers.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe aggregate fifty-three of them are plural yed as the divine truth, observant Savit─Б, (travels); the dicebow not before the wrath of any, however violent; a king himself pays them homage.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The aggregate…travels: asthe sun roams (viharati) in the world, so the heap of dice moves or plural ys on the dice table (─Бsph─Бre). Maybe,fifty-three dice were used, akс╣гik─Бс╕е pr─Бyeс╣Зa t─Бvadbhir akс╣гair d─лvyati, gamblers usually plural y with so manydice; maybe, the dice were thrown from east to west to render the comparison with the sun meaningful

Jamison Brereton

The troop of them plays, three times fifty strong. Like god SavitarтАЩs, their ordinances hold true.
Even to the battle fury of the mighty they do not bow; even the king makes his bow to them.

Griffith

Their troop of three-times-fifty plays [as undefeatably] as Savitr the god whose ways are faithful.
They bend not even to the anger of the mighty: the King himself pays homage and reveres them.

Macdonell

Their throng in triple fifties plays untrammelled, Like Savitar the god whose laws are constant. They yield not to the wrath of even the mighty: A king himself on them bestows obeisance.

Geldner

Ihre Schar tummelt sich dreimal f├╝nfzig z├дhlend, ihre Regeln sind g├╝ltig wie die des Gottes Savit?. Sie beugen sich nicht vor dem Zorn auch der Gewaltigen; auch der K├╢nig macht ihnen eine Verbeugung.

Grassmann

Es tummelt sich die Schar der dreiundfunfzig, wie Savitar, der Gott, die Ordnung wahrend, Sie weichen nicht dem Zorn, auch des gewalt’gen, ein K├╢nig selbst muss sich vor ihnen beugen.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬNow they abide below; now they palpitate on high handless, they overpower him who has hands; castupon the dice-board like coals from the sky, even though cold they burn the heart.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Downward they roll; up above they ricochet. Lacking hands, they overpower the man with hands.
Heavenly coals scattered down in the gaming hollow, though they are cold they burn up the heart.

Griffith

Downward they roll, and then spring quickly upward, and, handless, force the man with hands to serve them.
Cast on the board, like lumps of magic charcoal, though cold themselves they burn the heart to ashes.

Macdonell

Downward they roll, then swifty springing upward, They overcome the man with hands, though handless. Cast on the board like magic bits of charcoal, Though cold themselves, they burn the heart to ashes.

Geldner

Sie rollen nieder, schnellen in die H├╢he, ohne H├дnde zwingen sie dem, der H├дnde hat. Die ├╝berirdischen Kohlen, in die Rinne geworfen, versengen das Herz, obwohl sie kalt sind.

Grassmann

Sie rollen nieder, springen in die H├╢he, und handlos zwingen sie den handbegabten, Als Zauber-Kohlen auf die Bahn geworfen versengen sie das Herz, obwol sie kalt sind.

Elizarenkova

рд╕рд╛рдпрдг-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрдореН

рдХреНрд╡ рд╕реНрд╡рд┐рддреН рдХреНрд╡рд╛рдкрд┐ рдЪрд░рддрдГ рдирд┐рд░реНрд╡реЗрджрд╛рджреНрдЧрдЪреНрдЫрддрдГ рдХрд┐рддрд╡рд╕реНрдп рдЬрд╛рдпрд╛ рднрд╛рд░реНрдпрд╛ рд╣реАрдирд╛ рдкрд░рд┐рддреНрдпрдХреНрддрд╛ рд╕рддреА рддрдкреНрдпрддреЗ рд╡рд┐рдпреЛрдЧрдЬрд╕рдВрддрд╛рдкреЗрди рд╕рдВрддрдкреНрддрд╛ рднрд╡рддрд┐ред рдорд╛рддрд╛ рдЬрдирдиреНрдпрдкрд┐ рдкреБрддреНрд░рд╕реНрдп рдХреНрд╡рд╛рдкрд┐ рдЪрд░рддрдГ рдХрд┐рддрд╡рд╕реНрдп рд╕рдВрдмрдзрд╛рджреНрдзреАрдирд╛ рддрдкреНрдпрддреЗ ред рдкреБрддреНрд░рд╢реЛрдХреЗрди рд╕рдВрддрдкреНрддрд╛ рднрд╡рддрд┐ред рдЛрдгрд╛рд╡рд╛ рдЕрдХреНрд╖рдкрд░рд╛рдЬрдпрд╛рджреГрдгрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдХрд┐рддрд╡рдГ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рддреЛ рдмрд┐рднреНрдпрджреНрдзрдирдВ рд╕реНрддреЗрдпрдЬрдирд┐рддрдореН рдЗрдЪреНрдЫрдорд╛рдирдГ рдХрд╛рдордпрдорд╛рдирдГ рдЕрдиреНрдпреЗрд╖рд╛рдВ рдмреНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдордгрд╛рджреАрдирд╛рдореН рдЕрд╕реНрддрдВ рдЧреГрд╣рдоред тАШ рдЕрд╕реНрддрдВ рдкрд╕реНрддреНрдпрдореН ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рдЧреГрд╣рдирд╛рдорд╕реБ рдкрд╛рдард╛рддреН ред рдирдХреНрддрдВ рд░рд╛рддреНрд░реМ рдЙрдк рдРрддрд┐ рдЪреМрд░реНрдпрд╛рд░реНрдердореБрдкрдЧрдЪреНрдЫрддрд┐ рее рее рек рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe deserted wife of the gamester is afflicted; the mother (grieves) for the son wandering wherever helikes; involved in debt, ever in fear, anxious for wealth, (the gambler) goes forth by night to the dwellings of others(to plural nder).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The wife of the gambler, abandoned, is scorched, and the mother of the child wandering who knows where.
In debt, fearful, seeking money, he approaches by night the house of others.

Griffith

The gambler’s wife is left forlorn and wretched: the mother mourns the son who wanders homeless.
In constant fear, in debt, and seeking money, he goes by night to the home of others [probably to steal].

Macdonell

Grieved is the gambler’s wife by him abandoned, Grieved, too, his mother as he aimless wanders. Indebted, fearing, he desiring money At night approaches other people’s houses.

Geldner

Verlassen h├дrmt sich des Spielers Weib, die Mutter des Sohnes, der wer wei├Я wo hingeht. Verschuldet geht er voll Furcht Geld suchend bei der Nacht in das Haus anderer.

Grassmann

Verlassen gr├дmt des Spielers Weib sich einsam, die Mutter um den Sohn, wo mag er schweifen? Verschuldet, angstvoll und nach Gut verlangend geht er zur Nacht in andrer Leute Wohnung.

Elizarenkova

рдХрд┐рддрд╡рдВ рдХрд┐рддрд╡рдГ ред рд╡рд┐рднрдХреНрддрд┐рд╡реНрдпрддреНрдпрдпрдГ ред рдЕрдиреНрдпреЗрд╖рд╛рдВ рд╕реНрд╡рд╡реНрдпрддрд┐рд░рд┐рдХреНрддрд╛рдирд╛рдВ рдкреБрд░реБрд╖рд╛рдгрд╛рдВ рдЬрд╛рдпрд╛рдВ рдЬрд╛рдпрд╛рднреВрддрд╛рдВ рд╕реНрддреНрд░рд┐рдпрдВ рдирд╛рд░реАрдВ рд╕реБрдЦреЗрди рд╡рд░реНрддрдорд╛рдирд╛рдВ рд╕реБрдХреГрддрдВ рд╕реБрд╖реНрдареБ рдХреГрддрдВ рдпреЛрдирд┐рдВ рдЧреГрд╣рдВ рдЪ рджреГрд╖реНрдЯреНрд╡рд╛рдп рдордЬреНрдЬрд╛рдпрд╛ рджреБрдГрдЦрд┐рддрд╛ рдЧреГрд╣рдВ рдЪрд╛рд╕рдВрд╕реНрдХреГрддрдорд┐рддрд┐ рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рддреНрд╡рд╛ рддрддрд╛рдк рддрдкреНрдпрддреЗ ред рдкреБрдирдГ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╛рд╣реНрдгреЗ рдкреНрд░рд╛рддрдГрдХрд╛рд▓реЗ рдмрднреНрд░реВрдиреН рдмрднреНрд░реБрд╡рд░реНрдгрд╛рдиреН рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдкрдХрд╛рдирдХреНрд╖рд╛рдиреН рдпреБрдпреБрдЬреЗ рдпреБрдирдХреНрддрд┐ ред рдкреБрдирд╢реНрдЪ рд╡реГрд╖рд▓: рд╡реГрд╖рд▓рдХрд░реНрдорд╛ рд╕рдГ рдХрд┐рддрд╡реЛ рд░рд╛рддреНрд░реМ рдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗрд░рдиреНрддреЗ рд╕рдореАрдкреЗ рдкрдкрд╛рдж рд╢реАрддрд╛рд░реНрддрдГ рд╕рдиреН рд╢реЗрддреЗ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe gamester, having observed the happy wife and well-ordered home of others, suffers regret; yet inthe forenoon he puts to the tawny steeds, and at night the sinner lies down by the fire.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

It scorched the gambler to see a womanтАФthe wife and well-ordered home of others.
Since early in the day he hitched up his brown horses [=dice], the тАЬlittle bullockтАЭ fell [=left off gambling and sought shelter] (only) at the end of the fire [=late at night].

Griffith

Sad is the gambler when he sees a woman, another man’s wife, and his well-ordered dwelling.
He yokes the brown horses [= the dice] in the early morning, and in the evening he sinks down beside [his] fire, a beggar.

Macdonell

It pains the gambler when he sees a woman Another’s wife, and their well-ordered household. He yokes those brown steeds early in the morning, And when the fire is low sinks down a beggar.

Geldner

Es peinigt den Spieler, als er das Eheweib und das wohlbereitete Lager anderer sah. Da er schon am Vormittag die braunen Rosse angespannt hatte, so sank er elend in der N├дhe des Feuers nieder:

Grassmann

Es schmerzt den Spieler, wenn er nur ein Weib sieht, die Gattin und den sch├╢nen Heimsitz andrer; Die braunen W├╝rfel schirrt er fr├╝h am Morgen und sp├дt am Feuer sinkt er kraftlos nieder.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬDice, I offer salutation to him who has been the genitive ral of your great army, the chief lord of your host;I do not provide him with wealth; I raise my ten (fingers) to the east; that (which) I speak (is) the truth.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

I do notprovide him wealth: na dan─Б ruс╣Зadhmi = I do not withhold my wealth; na samp─Бday─Бmi

Jamison Brereton

[Gambler:] He who has become the general of your great throng, the foremost king of the troop,
to him I put forth my ten (fingers): тАЬI withhold no money. This truth I speak.тАЭ

Griffith

To the great captain of your mighty army [of dice], who has become the host’s imperial leader,
To him I show [my] ten [extended fingers]: “I speak the truth: No wealth am I withholding.”

Macdonell

To him who’s general of your mighty forces, As king becomes the chief of your battalions, I hold my fingers ten extended forward “No money I withhold, this truth I tell thee.”

Geldner

Wer der Heerf├╝hrer eurer gro├Яen Truppe, der oberste K├╢nig des Heerhaufens geworden ist, dem strecke ich die zehn Finger entgegen und schw├╢re einen Eid: Ich halte keine Sch├дtze zur├╝ck.

Grassmann

Ihm, der der F├╝hrer eures grossen Heeres und erster K├╢nig ist der ganzen Bande, Dem will ich meine Gaben nicht versagen, die Finger streck’ ich aus, beschw├╢r’ als wahr es.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬGiving serious attention (to my advie), plural y not with dice; pursue agriculture; delight in wealth (soacquired); there, gambler, are cows; there is a wife; so has this (visible) sovereign Savit─Б declared to me.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Their: there, i.e., in agriculture

Jamison Brereton

[Savitar:] тАЬDonтАЩt keep playing with dice; just plow your own plowland. Be content in your possessions, thinking them much.
There are your cows, o gambler, there your wife.тАЭ In this way does
Savitar here, protector of the stranger, watch out for me.

Griffith

“Play not with dice, [but] cultivate your corn-land. Enjoy the gain, and deem that wealth sufficient.
There are your cattle, there your wife, O gambler”: So this good Savitr himself has told me.

Macdonell

Play not with dice, but cultivate thy tillage, Enjoy thy riches, deeming them abundant. There are thy cows, there is thy wife, O Gambler: This counsel Savitar the noble gives me.

Geldner

Spiele nicht mehr mit den W├╝rfeln, bestelle deinen Acker; begn├╝ge dich mit deinem Besitz, ihn hoch haltend! Da sind deine Rinder, o Spieler, da dein Weib. Dies tut mir dieser Savit?, der Herr, kund.

Grassmann

┬╗Gib auf das Spiel, und pfl├╝ge deinen Acker, geniesse, was du hast, und halt’s in Ehren, Dann, Spieler, kommst zur Gattin du, zu Heerden┬л, So spricht zu mir Gott Savitar, der treue.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬBe friends with us (dice); bestow upon us happiness; approach us not in terrible wrath; let your angerlight upon our enemies; let our enemy fall under the bondage of the tawny (dice).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Let your anger light upon ourenemies: let your hostile wrath against us settle down, i.e., grow calm, cease

Jamison Brereton

[To all the dice:] Make alliance (with us) now; have pity on us. Do not conjure against us boldly with your terrible (mind/eye).
Let your battle fury now settle down, your hostility. Let another now be in the toils of the brown ones.
The next four hymns (35тАУ38) form a group, though they are not all attributed to the same author (see Oldenberg 1888: 229 n. 2, 235). The first two, to the All Gods, are attributed to Lu┼Ыa Dh─Бn─Бka, while the other two were given fanciful poetsтАЩ names derived from the contents of the hymn itself: 37 Abhitapas Saurya (тАЬScorching Heat, son of the SunтАЭ) and 38 Indra Muс╣гkavant (тАЬIndra, possessing testiclesтАЭ).

Griffith

Make me your friend: show us some little mercy. Do not forcibly bewitch us with magic power.
Let your wrath [and] emnity now come to rest. Let the brown [dice] now snare some other captive.

Macdonell

Make friends with us, we pray, to us be gracious; Do not bewitch us forcibly with magic; Let now your enmity, your anger slumber: Let others be in brownies’ toils entangled.

Geldner

Schlie├Яet also Freundschaft und erbarmet euch! Tut es uns nicht mehr dreist mit eurem schrecklichen Zauber an! Euer Groll und eure Ungunst soll sich jetzt legen; ein anderer soll jetzt in den Banden der Braunen sein!

Grassmann

So schliesst denn Frieden und erbarmt euch meiner, ergreift mich nicht mit eurem grausen Zauber; Es weiche eure Wuth nun, eure Feindschaft, der W├╝rfel Macht erliege nun ein andrer.

Elizarenkova

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдорд┐рддреНрд░рдВ рдХреГрдгреБрдзреНрд╡рдВ рдЦрд▓реБ) рд╣реЗ рдкреБрд░рд╛рдиреЗ рд╕рд╛рдереА рдЬреБрдЖрд░рд┐рдпреЛрдВ ! рддреБрдо рд▓реЛрдЧ рдореБрдЭреЗ рдорд┐рддреНрд░ рдмрдирд╛рдУ-рджреНрдпреВрддрдХрд╛рд░реНрдп рд╕реЗ рдореИрдВ рд╡рд┐рд░рдХреНрдд рд╣реЛ рдЧрдпрд╛, рдРрд╕рд╛ рдЬрд╛рдирдХрд░ рдореБрдЭрд╕реЗ рджреНрд╡реЗрд╖ рди рдХрд░реЛ рдФрд░ рдореЗрд░реЗ рдКрдкрд░ рдХреГрдкрд╛ рдмрдирд╛рдпреЗ рд░рдЦреЛ (рдирдГ-рдореГрд│рддрдГ) рд╣рдореЗрдВ рд╕реБрдЦреА рдХрд░реЛ (рдирдГ-рдШреЛрд░реЗрдг рдзреГрд╖реНрдгреБ рдорд╛ рдЪрд░рдд) рд╣рдорд╛рд░реЗ рдкреНрд░рддрд┐ рднрдпрдВрдХрд░ рджрдмрд╛рд╡ рд╕реЗ рди рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддреЛ(рд╡рдГ-рдордиреНрдпреБрдГ-рдиреБ рд╡рд┐рд╢рддрд╛рдореН) рддреБрдореНрд╣рд╛рд░рд╛ рдХреНрд░реЛрдз рддреБрдореНрд╣рд╛рд░реЗ рдЕрдиреНрджрд░ рд╣реА рд╡рд┐рд▓реАрди рд░рд╣реЗ (рдЕрдиреНрдпрдГ-рдЕрд░рд╛рддрд┐рдГ-рдмрднреНрд░реВрдгрд╛рдВ рдкреНрд░рд╕рд┐рддреМ рдиреБ-рдЕрд╕реНрддреБ) рдЕрдиреНрдп рдХреЛрдИ рд╡рдЮреНрдЪрдХ-рдЪреМрд░ рдЪрдордХрддреЗ рд╣реБрдП рдкрд╛рд╢реЛ рдХреЗ рдмрдиреНрдзрди рдореЗрдВ рдмрджреНрдз рд╣реЛрд╡реЗ реерезрекрее

рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордореБрдирд┐ - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЬреБрдЖ рдЦреЗрд▓рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓рд╛ рдЬреБрдП рдЦреЗрд▓рдиреЗ рдХреЗ рджреЛрд╖рджрд░реНрд╢рди рд╕реЗ рд╡рд┐рд░рдХреНрдд рд╣реЛ рдЬрд╛рддрд╛ рд╣реИ, рддреЛ рдЙрд╕рдХреЗ рдкреБрд░рд╛рдиреЗ рд╕рд╛рдереА рджреНрд╡реЗрд╖ рдХрд░рдиреЗ рд▓рдЧрддреЗ рд╣реИрдВред рд╡рд╣ рдЙрдиреНрд╣реЗрдВ рд╕рдордЭрд╛рд╡реЗ рдХрд┐ рд╡реЗ рдорд┐рддреНрд░рднрд╛рд╡ рдХрд░рдиреЗ рд▓рдЧреЗрдВ рдФрд░ рдХреЛрдИ рднреА рдЬреБрдП рдХреЗ рдмрдиреНрдзрди рдореЗрдВ рди рдлрдБрд╕реЗ реерезрекрее

рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордореБрдирд┐ - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдорд┐рддреНрд░рдВ рдХреГрдгреБрдзреНрд╡рдВ рдЦрд▓реБ) рд╣реЗ рдХрд┐рддрд╡рд╛рдГ ! рдпреВрдпрдВ рдЦрд▓реБ рдорд╛рдВ рдорд┐рддреНрд░рдВ рдХреБрд░реБрдд рджреНрдпреВрддрдХрд╛рд░реНрдпрддреЛрд╜рд╣рдВ рд╡рд┐рд░рдХреНрдд рдЗрддрд┐ рд▓рдХреНрд╖реНрдпреАрдХреГрддреНрдп рдорд╛рдВ рдкреНрд░рддрд┐ рджреНрд╡реЗрд╖рдВ рди рдХреБрд░реБрддрд╛рдкрд┐ рдордпрд┐ рдореИрддреНрд░реАрдВ рднрд╛рд╡рдпрдд рдордореЛрдкрд░рд┐ рдХреГрдкрд╛рдВ рд╡рд┐рдзрддреНрдд (рдирдГ рдореГрд│рдд) рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдиреН рд╕реБрдЦрдпрдд (рдирдГ рдШреЛрд░реЗрдг рдзреГрд╖реНрдгреБ рдорд╛ рдЪрд░рдд) рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдиреН рднрдпрдЩреНрдХрд░реЗрдг тАЬрдзреГрд╖реНрдгреБрдирд╛тАЭ рддреГрддреАрдпрд╛рд╡рд┐рднрдХреНрддреЗрд░реНрд▓реБрдХреН рдзрд░реНрд╖рдгрдмрд▓реЗрди рди рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдзреНрд╡рдореН (рд╡рдГ-рдордиреНрдпреБрдГ-рдиреБ рд╡рд┐рд╢рддрд╛рдореН) рдпреБрд╖реНрдорд╛рдХрдВ рдХреНрд░реЛрдзреЛ рдпреБрд╖реНрдорд╛рдХрдордиреНрддрд░реЗ рд╣рд┐ рдирд┐рд╡рд┐рд╖реНрдЯрд╕реНрддрд┐рд╖реНрдарддреБ (рдЕрдиреНрдпрдГ-рдЕрд░рд╛рддрд┐рдГ-рдмрднреНрд░реВрдгрд╛рдВ рдкреНрд░рд╕рд┐рддреМ рдиреБ рдЕрд╕реНрддреБ) рдЕрдиреНрдпреЛрд╜рджрд╛рддрд╛ рд╡рдЮреНрдЪрдХрд╢реНрдЪреМрд░реЛ рдмрднреНрд░реБрд╡рд░реНрдгрд╛рдирд╛рдордХреНрд╖рд╛рдгрд╛рдВ рджреНрдпреВрддрд╕рд╛рдзрдирд╛рдирд╛рдВ рдмрдиреНрдзрдиреЗ рдЬрд╛рд▓реЗтАЬрдкреНрд░рд╕рд┐рддрд┐рдГ рдкреНрд░рд╕рдпрдирд╛рддреН рддрдиреНрддреБрд░реНрд╡рд╛ рдЬрд╛рд▓рдВ рд╡рд╛тАЭ[ рдирд┐рд░реБрежремредрезреи] рдмрджреНрдзреЛ рднрд╡рддреБ реерезрекрее
